<a id="A"></a>

## A)

---

<b>Word:</b> Accountability

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ú‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶π‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶æ (‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¶‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶¨‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Responsibility, Answerability, Liability, Compliance.

<b>English Example:</b> "I destroyed their logs to erase any sense of accountability; now the sysadmins have no way to prove who triggered the system wipe." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡¶ó‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶Ç‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ú‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶π‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ (Accountability) ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶â‡¶™‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, accountability ensures that every action on a network can be traced back to a specific user or process. It is the "A" in the AAA Framework (Authentication, Authorization, and Accountability). Without robust logging and auditing, you cannot hold anyone responsible for a security breach.

---

<b>Word:</b> Accumulate

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ú‡¶Æ‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶π ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶ß‡ßÄ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ß‡ßÄ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßÉ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Amass, Collect, Gather, Stockpile.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôve been letting the keylogger run for weeks to accumulate a massive stash of bank logins before I start the wire transfers." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶π ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡¶ó‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶£‡ßç‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶Æ‡¶æ (Accumulate) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, "accumulate" often refers to the data collection phase of an attack. Hackers accumulate information‚Äîsuch as network logs, user behaviors, or credentials‚Äîover time to ensure that when they finally strike, they have enough data to bypass security or maximize the impact of the breach.

---

<b>Word:</b> Aesthetic

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective / Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßå‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ß (‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Visual style, Artistic, Appearance, Look.

<b>English Example:</b> "I don't just deface websites; I give them a dark, glitch-art aesthetic so they know exactly which group wrecked their servers." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶ß‡ßÅ ‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ü ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶´‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶æ; ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ì ‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ö-‡¶Ü‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶§‡¶æ (Aesthetic) ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶á ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßÅ‡¶ù‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶® ‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶™ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶Ç‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In the hacker subculture, "aesthetic" often refers to the visual identity of a group or the UI of their tools (like specialized Linux distros or terminal themes). While it doesn't affect the technical success of an exploit, a distinct aesthetic is used in "defacement" attacks to leave a digital signature and build a reputation in the underground community.

---

<b>Term:</b> Black Aesthetic

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶è‡¶∏‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶ú‡¶ó‡¶§‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∞‡¶π‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßü ‡¶•‡¶ø‡¶Æ, ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶® ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßü)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Dark mode style, Cyberpunk look, Underground hacker vibe.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôve customized my terminal with a sleek black aesthetic and toxic green fonts to feel like a ghost while I‚Äôm navigating their internal network." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡¶∏‡ßÉ‡¶£ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶è‡¶∏‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï (Black Aesthetic) ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∑‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶∏‡¶¨‡ßÅ‡¶ú ‡¶´‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ò‡ßã‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ú‡¶® ‡¶≠‡ßÇ‡¶§‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶π‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity culture, "Black Aesthetic" refers to the visual preference for dark interfaces. Beyond just looking "cool" or "edgy," this aesthetic is practical; dark modes reduce eye strain during long hours of night-time coding and monitoring. It has become synonymous with the "hacker vibe" often seen in terminal themes and specialized operating systems like Kali Linux.

---

<b>Word:</b> Attribution

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¶‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶¨‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶â‡ßé‡¶∏ ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶õ‡ßá‚Äî‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶® ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶® ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‚Äî‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶π‡ßç‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Identification, Assignment, Credit, Source tracing.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "I‚Äôve used three layers of proxies and spoofed a Russian APT's signature to make sure the forensic team's attribution points in the wrong direction." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶® ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶® APT-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶´‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∏ ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ (Attribution) ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡¶≤ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Attribution is the process of tracking and identifying the person or group responsible for a cyberattack. It is notoriously difficult because attackers use techniques like false flags, VPNs, and compromised servers in other countries to hide their identity. In high-level cybersecurity, attribution is used to decide on legal actions or international sanctions.

---

<b>Term:</b> Delayed Attribution

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶â‡ßé‡¶∏ ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ (‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤ ‡¶π‡ßã‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü, ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßü ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶ú‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Retrospective identification, Post-facto attribution, Lagged source tracing.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "By the time they finish their analysis for a delayed attribution, I‚Äôll have laundered the crypto and vanished into a non-extradition country." (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶â‡ßé‡¶∏ ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ (Delayed attribution) ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá, ‡¶§‡¶§‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ø ‡¶≤‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶¨ ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶¨ ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Delayed Attribution occurs when an attacker uses sophisticated evasion techniques‚Äîsuch as dormant code, multi-hop proxies, or "Living off the Land" (LotL) binaries‚Äîto mask their identity. This forces investigators to spend months or even years piecing together evidence. In many cases, by the time the attribution is confirmed, the tactical or political window for a response has already closed.

---

<b>Word:</b> Amplified

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Past Tense / Past Participle) / Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÅ‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶£ ‡¶¨‡ßÉ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∂‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡ßú‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Magnified, Intensified, Boosted, Escalated.

<b>Example:</b> "I used a misconfigured DNS server to send an amplified blast of traffic at their site, knocking it offline in seconds." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶®‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ DNS ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£ (Amplified) ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶´‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u>
In cybersecurity, an Amplification Attack is a form of DDoS (Distributed Denial of Service). The attacker sends a small request to a server (like DNS or NTP) using a spoofed IP address, and the server responds with a much larger packet to the victim. This "amplifies" the bandwidth consumed, allowing a single hacker to overwhelm a massive network.

---

<b>Word:</b> Annotate

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶π ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Comment, Note, Mark up, Label.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôm going to annotate this source code to mark every weak function before I launch the exploit script." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶∏‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶°‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶π ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶ü (Annotate) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶≤ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Ç‡¶∂‡¶® ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶π‡ßç‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, annotation is critical during Reverse Engineering or Malware Analysis. Security analysts annotate disassembled code to keep track of what different sections of a virus do. Conversely, attackers annotate their reconnaissance data to organize targets and vulnerabilities for a more efficient strike.

---

<b>Word:</b> Apprentice

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂ (‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶¶‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶ß‡ßÄ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶ñ‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Trainee, Novice, Learner, Rookie, Intern.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôm training a new apprentice to handle the botnet; he‚Äôs still a script-kiddie, but he‚Äôll be dropping payloads like a pro in a month." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶ü‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ú‡¶® ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ï‡ßá (Apprentice) ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶≤ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá, ‡¶§‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶° ‡¶°‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶™ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In the cybersecurity world, an Apprentice often refers to a junior analyst in a SOC (Security Operations Center) or a beginner in a hacking collective. On the dark web, veteran hackers often take on apprentices to scale their operations, teaching them how to conduct reconnaissance or maintain persistence in exchange for a cut of the profits.

---

<b>Word:</b> Assess

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶≤‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Evaluate, Analyze, Inspect, Examine.

<b>Example:</b> "I need to assess the strength of their firewall before I launch the exploit; if I find even one tiny crack, their whole network is toast." (‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∂‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶® (Assess) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá; ‡¶Ø‡¶¶‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶≤‡¶ì ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶á, ‡¶§‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, to assess is to conduct a Vulnerability Assessment. This is a systematic review of security weaknesses in an information system. It identifies, quantifies, and prioritizes vulnerabilities to ensure that the most critical "holes" are patched before a threat actor can exploit them.

---

<b>Word:</b> Asymmetric

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡¶Æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßÄ‡¶Ø‡¶º (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Ø‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶á ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∂‡ßá ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶® ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶® ‡¶™‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßÄ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Unbalanced, Disproportionate, Non-uniform, Public-key (in crypto context).

<b>English Example:</b> "I exploited the asymmetric encryption flaw; I used their own public key to encrypt the ransomware, knowing they‚Äôd never get the private key back without paying me." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∏ymmetric ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡¶∂‡¶® ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡ßÄ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶∞‚Äç‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø, ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶™‡¶£ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶õ‡¶æ‡ßú‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡ßÄ-‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶ñ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶á ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Asymmetric Encryption (also known as Public Key Cryptography) uses a pair of related keys: a Public Key for encryption and a Private Key for decryption. It is called asymmetric because the keys are different. This is the foundation of secure web browsing (HTTPS) and digital signatures.

---

<a id="B"></a>

## B)

---

<b>Word:</b> Backfire

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb / Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶â‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßã ‡¶´‡¶≤ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶§ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßÉ‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶™‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Rebound, Boomerang, Recoil, Self-defeat.

<b>English Example:</b> "I tried to wipe the server logs to hide my tracks, but it backfired and triggered a high-priority alert that locked me out of the system." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶π‡ßç‡¶® ‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡¶ó‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ö‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶Æ, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶â‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßã ‡¶´‡¶≤ (Backfire) ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶â‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶ö-‡¶∏‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶§ ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, a "backfire" occurs when an offensive tool or defensive script causes unintended self-damage. For example, poorly written ransomware might encrypt the hacker's own command server, or an aggressive firewall rule might accidentally block the legitimate admin's access.

---

<b>Word:</b> Bait

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶™ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶≠‡¶® (‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶¶‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßü)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Lure, Enticement, Trap, Decoy.

<b>Example:</b> "I left a few USB drives in the company parking lot as bait; as soon as a curious employee plugs one in, my malware will spread through their network like wildfire." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶≤‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶á‡¶â‡¶è‡¶∏‡¶¨‡¶ø ‡¶°‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≠ ‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶™ (Bait) ‡¶π‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ñ‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡ßå‡¶§‡ßÇ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßÄ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ ‡¶ì‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶ó ‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶õ‡¶°‡¶º‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶°‡¶º‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Baiting is a form of social engineering where an attacker leaves a physical object (like a USB) or a digital "gift" (like a free movie download) to trick a victim. The bait relies on human curiosity or greed. Once the victim takes the bait, the malicious payload is executed on their system.

---

<b>Word:</b> Beaconing

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶§ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÄ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Ö‡¶™‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Heartbeat, Call-back, Polling, C2 Communication.

<b>Example:</b> "The payload is silent for now, but the beaconing starts every ten minutes; it's just checking my C2 server to see if I‚Äôm ready to drop the ransomware." (‡¶™‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶°‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶™‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶™ ‡¶Ü‡¶õ‡ßá, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¶‡¶∂ ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶§ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã (Beaconing) ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá; ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶ß‡ßÅ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø-‡¶ü‡ßÅ (C2) ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶õ‡¶æ‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶æ‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Beaconing is the process where a compromised system "calls home" to a Command and Control (C2) server. It typically happens at regular intervals to bypass firewalls, as outbound traffic is often less scrutinized than inbound. Detecting these heartbeats is a key way for defenders to identify an infected machine within their network.

---

<b>Word:</b> Binge

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ö‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶Ö‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶™ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Spree, Overindulgence, Excess, Bouts.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôm going on a credential-stuffing binge tonight; I‚Äôve got ten million leaked passwords to burn through before the admins wake up." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶ú ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶°‡ßá‡¶®‡¶∂‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶≤-‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶æ‡ßü (Binge) ‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶â‡¶†‡¶¨; ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶ì‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¶‡¶∂ ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶® ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶π‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶Ü‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In a cyber context, a "binge" often describes a period of intense, rapid-fire activity. This could be a "download binge" during data exfiltration or a "vulnerability binge" where a researcher (or attacker) discovers and exploits multiple bugs in a single session before they can be patched.

---

<b>Term:</b> Binge scrolling

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü ‡¶®‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßÄ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ò‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Doomscrolling, Endless scrolling, Infinite browsing.

<b>English Example:</b> "While the target was busy binge scrolling through social media, my spyware was silently exfiltrating every private photo from their device." (‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶∏‡ßã‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶°‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤ (Binge scrolling) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤, ‡¶§‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶É‡¶∂‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∏ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶¨ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶§ ‡¶õ‡¶¨‡¶ø ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, binge scrolling is often linked to Social Engineering. Attackers exploit the distracted state of a user who is binge scrolling to slip in malicious ads (malvertising) or "clickbait" lures that the user might click impulsively without checking the URL or source.

---

<b>Word:</b> Bragging

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb (Gerund)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶≠‡ßã‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶ó‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Boasting, Vaunting, Show-off, Crowing.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "The hacker's downfall was his bragging on a public forum; he posted screenshots of the database he stole just to gain 'clout' among his peers." (‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶§‡¶® ‡¶π‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶´‡ßã‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ (Bragging) ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡ßá; ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶¨‡ßü‡¶∏‡ßÄ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶∂‡¶ü ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In the cybersecurity world, Bragging is a common trait of "Script Kiddies" or fame-driven hackers. While sophisticated groups (like APTs) prefer to stay quiet and maintain Dwell Time, less experienced hackers often post their successes on Twitter (X), Telegram, or underground forums to build their reputation. This ego-driven behavior is a goldmine for digital forensics teams and law enforcement, as it often leads to the Attribution and eventual arrest of the attacker.

---

<b>Term:</b> Public Bragging

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ú‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡ßà‡¶ß ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶•‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Overt boasting, Public vaunting, Open gloating, High-profile posturing.

<b>English Example:</b> "Your public bragging on Twitter attracted the feds' attention; now the whole operation is burned because you wanted some likes." (‡¶ü‡ßÅ‡¶á‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶ú‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶ó‡ßã‡ßü‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ú‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßá‡ßú‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ï ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In the cyberworld, public bragging occurs when threat actors claim responsibility for an attack on social media or public leak sites. While it builds a "brand" for the hacking group, it significantly increases the risk of attribution (being identified) as security agencies prioritize targets that cause public embarrassment or panic.

<b>Word:</b> Brochure

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡¶§ ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶≠‡¶®‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡¶ï ‡¶°‡¶ï‡ßÅ‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Pamphlet, Booklet, Leaflet, Prospectus.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "I‚Äôve embedded a malicious macro inside this fake corporate benefits brochure; one click to 'Enable Content' and I have a shell on their system." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ (Brochure) ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; '‡¶è‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü'-‡¶è ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡¶ñ‡¶≤ ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In a hacking context, a Brochure is often used as a "lure" in a Phishing or Spear-Phishing attack. Attackers send PDF or Word documents disguised as informative brochures (e.g., "Company Policy" or "Product Catalog") to trick users into downloading them. Once opened, these files execute hidden scripts to infect the victim's computer.chure

<b>Word:</b> Bootcamp

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶°‡¶º ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶∏‡ßÇ‡¶ö‡¶ø (‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶™ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∑‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∏)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Intensive training, Crash course, Fast-track program, Drill.

<b>English Example:</b> "Those script kiddies coming out of that six-week bootcamp think they‚Äôre pros, but they won‚Äôt even notice when I've backdoored their 'secure' lab environment." (‡¶õ‡ßü ‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶π‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶¨‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™ (Bootcamp) ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá, ‡¶Ö‡¶•‡¶ö ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞‡¶á ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ '‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞' ‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶¨ ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶∞‡¶®‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶°‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶∏‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In the tech and cybersecurity world, a bootcamp is an accelerated learning program designed to teach high-demand skills (like ethical hacking or SOC analysis) in a very short time. While they provide a fast track to entry-level jobs, real-world mastery often requires the deep, hands-on experience that bootcamps can only jumpstart.

<b>Word:</b> Bulk

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective / Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÇ‡¶™ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶π‡ßü)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Mass, Large-scale, Volume, Wholesale.

<b>Example:</b> "I just dumped a bulk list of a million stolen emails onto the dark web forum for the highest bidder." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶á‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶¨ ‡¶´‡ßã‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶ö ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¶‡¶∂ ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑ ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶á‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ (Bulk list) ‡¶õ‡ßá‡ßú‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, bulk usually refers to automated, large-scale operations. For example, "bulk data exfiltration" is the act of stealing massive amounts of data at once, or "bulk spamming" is used to distribute malware to thousands of targets simultaneously to increase the success rate.

---

<a id="C"></a>

## C)

---

<b>Word:</b> Cascade

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb / Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶™‡ßá ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶™‡ßá ‡¶ò‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶™‡¶§‡¶® (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ò‡¶ü‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∞‡¶ì ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ò‡¶ü‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ò‡¶ü‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Chain reaction, Domino effect, Sequence, Ripple.

<b>English Example:</b> "Once I cracked the master admin password, I triggered a cascade of failures that took down every satellite office in the network." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶®‡¶á ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶® ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶ô‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶Æ, ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶•‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∂‡ßÉ‡¶ô‡ßç‡¶ñ‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶° ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∏‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶ö‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, a Cascading Failure occurs when the failure of one node or component triggers a sequence of failures in other connected components. Attackers aim for this to maximize impact; for instance, compromising a central authentication server can cause access to cascade shut across an entire global infrastructure.

---

<b>Word:</b> Closure

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶® (‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡ßÇ‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Conclusion, Termination, Settlement, Resolution.

<b>English Example:</b> "The feds think they got closure by seizing my old server, but they don't realize I've already migrated the operation to a new cluster." (‡¶´‡ßá‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶ú‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶¶ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶® (Closure) ‡¶ò‡¶ü‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßÅ‡¶ù‡¶§‡ßá‡¶ì ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶§‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶® ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In a general technical context, Closure refers to the completion of a process. In programming (like JavaScript), a Closure is a function that remembers its outer variables even after the outer function has finished. From a security standpoint, "closure" can also refer to Incident Closure, where a security breach is officially resolved and documented after the threat is neutralized and the system is patched.

---

<b>Word:</b> Cognitive

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ú‡ßç‡¶û‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÄ‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ß‡¶∂‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø-‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ (‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ, ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶Æ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Intellectual, Mental, Analytical, Perceptive.

<b>Example:</b> "The attacker exploited a cognitive bias by making the email look like it came from a friend, causing the victim to trust it without thinking." (‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡ßç‡¶û‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÄ‡¶Ø‡¶º (Cognitive) ‡¶™‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‚Äî‡¶á‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶¨‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ß‡ßÅ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶õ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶´‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Cognitive Hacking refers to manipulating a person's perception of reality to change their behavior. It targets Cognitive Biases‚Äîshortcuts the human brain takes to process information. For example, the "Authority Bias" makes us more likely to follow instructions from someone who appears to be a boss, while the "Scarcity Principle" makes us act quickly when told a deal is about to expire.

---

<b>Word:</b> Counterfeit

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective / Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶≤ (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶â‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßÉ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Fake, Forged, Spurious, Bogus, Phony.

<b>Example:</b> "I replaced the original login script with a counterfeit version; now every user who logs in is unknowingly handing their credentials straight to my server." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤ ‡¶≤‡¶ó‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶≤ (Counterfeit) ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶® ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶¶‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶≤‡¶ó‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶®‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶°‡ßá‡¶®‡¶∂‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, counterfeit elements are used in "Spoofing" or "Cloning" attacks. This could be a counterfeit website (phishing), a counterfeit certificate, or even counterfeit hardware. The goal is to deceive a user or a system into trusting a fake entity to bypass security protocols.

---

<b>Word:</b> Credentials

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun (Plural)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßü‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶á‡¶â‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Login details, Auth tokens, Identification, Passcodes.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôve just phished the admin‚Äôs credentials; now the entire database is mine to bleed." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶á‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶°‡ßá‡¶®‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã (‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞) ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∏‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶Æ‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, credentials are the keys to the kingdom. They are the identity data (like passwords, keys, or biometrics) used to verify a user. Protecting them via MFA (Multi-Factor Authentication) is the primary defense against unauthorized access.

---

<a id="D"></a>

## D)

---

<b>Word:</b> Deanonymization

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∂ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßÄ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ó‡ßã‡¶™‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Unmasking, De-identification reversal, Re-identification.

<b>English Example:</b> "I cross-referenced the leaked metadata with public social profiles to perform a deanonymization of the target; now their 'anonymous' handle is linked straight to their home address." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶π‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡ßã‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßü ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∂ (Deanonymization) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ '‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßÄ' ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Deanonymization is the process of matching anonymous data with available information to discover the real identity of a user. In cybersecurity, it‚Äôs often used by attackers to unmask individuals behind encrypted or pseudonymized datasets by using data mining and pattern matching.

---

<b>Word:</b> Deceptive

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≠‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶∞ (‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶§‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶®‡ßü ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶∏‡¶§‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶π‡ßü)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Misleading, Fraudulent, Dishonest, Illusory.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôve set up a deceptive login page that looks identical to the bank‚Äôs portal; once the marks enter their pins, I‚Äôve got full control of their cash." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡¶ï (Deceptive) ‡¶≤‡¶ó‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶ú ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶π‡ßÅ‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÅ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã; ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶® ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶á, ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶¨ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Deceptive techniques are the core of "Deception Technology." This involves using decoys like honeypots or breadcrumbs to mislead attackers. Conversely, hackers use deceptive tactics in Social Engineering and Spoofing to trick victims into revealing secrets by mimicking trusted entities.

---

<b>Word:</b> Decoy

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶™ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶¶ (‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤ ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßå‡¶∂‡¶≤)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Bait, Distraction, Lure, Honey-pot, Camouflage.

<b>Example:</b> "I'll flood their SOC with a loud, obvious DDoS decoy; while their security team is busy fighting that ghost, I‚Äôll silently slip through the back door and grab the database." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßú ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶™‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶ì‡¶è‡¶∏ (DDoS) ‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶™ (Decoy) ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶¨; ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶≤ ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶¨‡ßá, ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶É‡¶∂‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶ú‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∏‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶¨‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, a Decoy can be used both offensively and defensively. Defenders use "Honeypots" as decoys to trap and study attackers. Conversely, attackers use decoys (like a noisy but harmless scan) to distract security systems while they perform a more sophisticated, silent attack elsewhere.

---

<b>Word:</b> Deepfake

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ï‡ßÉ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ ‡¶¨‡ßÅ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ (AI) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶¨ ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶ì, ‡¶Ö‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶ì ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶õ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Synthetic media, AI-generated forgery, Digital manipulation.

<b>Example:</b> "The attacker used a deepfake of the CEO's voice during the Zoom call to convince the finance manager to transfer five million dollars." (‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ ‡¶ú‡ßÅ‡¶Æ ‡¶ï‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶á‡¶ì-‡¶∞ (CEO) ‡¶ï‡¶£‡ßç‡¶†‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶™‡¶´‡ßá‡¶ï (Deepfake) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶∏ ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶ö ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶® ‡¶°‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Deepfakes represent the next evolution of social engineering. By using Generative AI, attackers can create highly convincing video or audio clones of trusted individuals. This makes traditional verification methods (like "I recognize their voice") unreliable. Defending against deepfakes requires multi-factor authentication and specialized AI tools that can detect subtle inconsistencies in digital media

---

<b>Word:</b> DNS Tunneling

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶è‡¶®‡¶è‡¶∏ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶Ç (‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶è‡¶®‡¶è‡¶∏ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶ï‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶®-‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶´‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßå‡¶∂‡¶≤)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> DNS data exfiltration, C2 over DNS, Protocol encapsulation.

<b>Example:</b> "Their firewall is high-end, but it‚Äôs not inspecting DNS queries; I‚Äôll use DNS tunneling to sneak the stolen passwords out byte-by-byte through their own name servers." (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶¨ ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶è‡¶®‡¶è‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ; ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶è‡¶®‡¶è‡¶∏ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶Ç (DNS tunneling) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶™ ‡¶Ö‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶™ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶¨‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> DNS Tunneling exploits the fact that DNS traffic is usually allowed through firewalls without deep inspection. Attackers encode data or commands into DNS queries and responses. It is primarily used for stealthy command-and-control (C2) communication or "Data Exfiltration" (stealing data) from highly restricted networks.

---

<b>Word:</b> DNS Lookup

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶è‡¶®‡¶è‡¶∏ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∏‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶® (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶°‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∏‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶™‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶∞‡ßÇ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> DNS resolution, Address translation, Hostname-to-IP query.

<b>Example:</b> "Before I hijack their traffic, I‚Äôll perform a DNS lookup to pinpoint the exact IP of their web server and check if they're using a proxy I can exploit." (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ú‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá, ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶è‡¶®‡¶è‡¶∏ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∏‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶® (DNS lookup) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßá‡¶¨ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶™‡¶ø ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> A DNS Lookup is like looking up a phone number in a directory. Computers communicate via IP addresses (like 192.168.1.1), but humans use domain names (like example.com). DNS lookups bridge this gap. Attackers often use them for reconnaissance to map out a target‚Äôs infrastructure.

---

<b>Word:</b> Disguised

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Past Tense / Past Participle) / Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶õ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂ ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∞‡ßÇ‡¶™ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Concealed, Masked, Hidden, Camouflaged.

<b>Example:</b> "The malware was disguised as a simple PDF invoice, but once opened, it began encrypting every file on the hard drive." (‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶è‡¶´ (PDF) ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶≠‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶õ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂ ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ (Disguised) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶ñ‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶°‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤ ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, disguising is the core concept behind a Trojan Horse. Just like the Greek myth, a Trojan is a malicious program that is disguised as legitimate software (like a free game or a system utility). Another common method is File Extension Disguise, where a file named report.pdf.exe appears to be a document but is actually an executable virus.

---

<b>Word:</b> Dwell

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡¶§ ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßú‡ßá ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ‡ßü)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Reside, Inhabit, Linger, Persist.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "The rootkit allowed the attacker to dwell in the company's mainframe for six months before the first suspicious packet was flagged." (‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶á‡¶®‡¶´‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶õ‡ßü ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ (Dwell) ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤, ‡¶Ø‡¶§‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶•‡¶Æ ‡¶∏‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶π‡¶ú‡¶®‡¶ï ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßú‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, you will most commonly see this word in the term Dwell Time. This is the duration between when an attacker first gains access to a system and when they are finally detected and evicted. A high dwell time is dangerous because it gives hackers more than enough time to steal data, escalate privileges, and plant "backdoors" for future access. Reducing dwell time is a top priority for SOC (Security Operations Center) teams.

---

<b>Term:</b> Dwell Time

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶≤ (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ú‡¶® ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü‡¶ü‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßÅ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Retention time, Presence duration, Latency period.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "The average dwell time for state-sponsored attacks is often over 200 days, giving hackers plenty of time to siphon off sensitive data." (‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶Æ‡¶¶‡¶¶‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ó‡ßú ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶≤ (Dwell time) ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶á ‡ß®‡ß¶‡ß¶ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶ø ‡¶π‡ßü, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶¶‡¶®‡¶∂‡ßÄ‡¶≤ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü ‡¶¶‡ßá‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Dwell Time is a critical metric in cybersecurity. It is calculated as the time elapsed between the Initial Infection and Detection.

Mean Time to Detect (MTTD): The average time it takes to realize an intruder is present.

Mean Time to Respond (MTTR): The time it takes to kick the hacker out after they are found. A long dwell time indicates that the organization's monitoring tools are failing, allowing attackers to perform "lateral movement" and "privilege escalation" undisturbed.

---

<a id="E"></a>

## E)

---

<b>Word:</b> Emerged

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Past Tense)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ü‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡ßÇ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∂ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ (‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶π‡ßÅ‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Appeared, Surfaced, Materialized, Revealed.

<b>Example:</b> "A new zero-day vulnerability just emerged in the latest OS patch, and I'm already coding an exploit to hit them before they can fix it." (‡¶Ö‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö-‡¶è ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶ú‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßã-‡¶°‡ßá ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∂ ‡¶™‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá (Emerged), ‡¶Ü‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶ò‡¶æ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶° ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, the term is often used for Emerging Threats. This refers to newly identified risks, such as a novel strain of malware or a previously unknown software bug (Zero-day). Security teams must monitor threat intelligence feeds to catch these threats as soon as they have emerged to prevent large-scale exploitation.

---

<b>Word:</b> Entropy

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßÉ‡¶ô‡ßç‡¶ñ‡¶≤‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶ö‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶§‡¶æ (‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∞‚Äç‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨ ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡¶∂‡¶® ‡¶ï‡ßÄ-‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∂‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßÄ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Randomness, Disorder, Uncertainty, Chaos.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "Your password has zero entropy; it took my brute-force script less than a second to crack that predictable string." (‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶™‡¶ø (Entropy) ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ú‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶á; ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü-‡¶´‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∏ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞‡¶ì ‡¶ï‡¶Æ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Entropy is a measure of the randomness or unpredictability of data. High entropy is crucial for encryption keys and passwords because it makes them resistant to guessing or brute-force attacks. If a system's entropy is low (predictable), an attacker can easily calculate the "random" values used for security, breaking the entire encryption.

---

b>Word:</b> Eventual

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ö‡ßÇ‡¶°‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶£‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßÇ‡¶™ (‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ò‡¶ü‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶á)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Final, Ultimate, Concluding, Resulting.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "The bug I planted is small, but the eventual system crash is inevitable once the memory leak reaches its limit." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßã‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßÄ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶™‡ßå‡¶Å‡¶õ‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá, ‡¶§‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡ßÇ‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ (Eventual) ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∂ ‡¶π‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity and distributed systems, you might often hear the term Eventual Consistency. This means that even if data isn't updated everywhere instantly, it is guaranteed that all access to that data will eventually return the last updated value. From an attacker's perspective, "eventual" often refers to the long-term goal of an attack, such as an APT (Advanced Persistent Threat) that waits patiently for the eventual moment to strike.

---

<b>Word:</b> Executives

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun (Plural)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶â‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶ö‡¶™‡¶¶‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶• ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶π‡ßÄ (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶®: CEO, CFO ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡¶ó‡¶£)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Corporate leaders, Top brass, Management, Decision-makers.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôve been monitoring the executives' travel schedules to time my spear-phishing attack when they‚Äôre distracted at a tech conference." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶â‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶ö‡¶™‡¶¶‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶• ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ (Executives) ‡¶≠‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü‡¶∏‡ßÇ‡¶ö‡ßÄ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶®‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶¨‡ßá, ‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞-‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Executives are often referred to as "High-Value Targets" (HVTs). Because they have broad access to sensitive corporate data and the authority to approve large financial transactions, they are the primary targets for Whaling and Business Email Compromise (BEC) attacks. Securing their accounts with hardware tokens and strict verification protocols is critical for organizational safety.

---

<b>Word:</b> Exfiltration

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶õ‡¶æ‡ßú‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Data theft, Extraction, Smuggling, Removal.

<b>English Example:</b> "The exfiltration is almost complete; while their IT team was busy chasing a fake DDoS attack, I quietly tunneled five terabytes of their customer data out to my offshore server." (‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ (Exfiltration) ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑; ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶ì‡¶è‡¶∏ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤, ‡¶§‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶É‡¶∂‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶ö ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶´‡¶∂‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Data Exfiltration is the unauthorized transfer of data from a computer or other device. It can be done manually via physical media (like USBs) or over a network using various protocols. Hackers often use "stealthy" channels (like DNS or HTTP) to hide the exfiltration process from firewalls and monitoring tools.

---

<b>Word:</b> Exhaust

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶É‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡ßÇ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£ ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶æ (‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶£‡ßç‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∂‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Deplete, Drain, Consume, Use up.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôll keep flooding their server with junk traffic until I exhaust their bandwidth and the whole system crashes." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ú‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶¨ ‡¶Ø‡¶§‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡¶â‡¶á‡¶• ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶É‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∂ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, "exhaustion attacks" (like Resource Exhaustion) aim to consume a system's limited resources‚Äîsuch as CPU, memory, or disk space. A common example is a DoS (Denial of Service) attack, where the attacker exhausts the target's capacity to handle requests, making the service unavailable to legitimate users.

---

<a id="F"></a>

## F)

---

<b>Word:</b> Fledged

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßÇ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶™‡ßÇ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£‡¶æ‡¶ô‡ßç‡¶ó ‡¶∞‡ßÇ‡¶™ ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶≠ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Fully developed, Mature, Complete, Full-scale.

<b>English Example:</b> "I started with a simple script, but now it‚Äôs a full-fledged ransomware strain capable of locking down an entire corporate infrastructure in seconds." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶Æ, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßÇ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶§ (Full-fledged) ‡¶∞‚Äç‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßã ‡¶≤‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶Æ‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In a technical context, "full-fledged" describes software or an attack that has moved from the prototype or "Proof of Concept" (PoC) stage to a complete, stable, and fully functional version. For example, a full-fledged malware includes all components like a dropper, payload, and C2 communication module.

---

<b>Word:</b> Freak

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb / Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ü‡¶ö‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Ø‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∏ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Glitch, Malfunction, Outrage, Deviate.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "I sent a series of malformed packets to the firewall just to make it freak out and drop all its security rules." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßÇ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ü‡¶ö‡¶∞‡¶£ (Freak out) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶¨ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶≤ ‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In a technical or hacker context, to freak or "freak out" means to cause a system to enter an unstable or unintended state. This is often the goal of Fuzzing (sending random data to an input), where the attacker tries to find bugs by seeing what inputs make the software "freak" and crash, potentially revealing a vulnerability.

---

<a id="G"></a>

## G)

---

<b>Word:</b> Gamified

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective / Verb (Past Participle)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶Ü‡¶®‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶¶‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶â‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£‡ßÄ‡ßü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Ludified, Incentivized, Game-based, Competitive.

<b>English Example:</b> "The company gamified their security training with badges and leaderboards, but I still found a way to social engineer the 'top player' into giving up his token." (‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶Æ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶∞ (Gamified) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶á ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ '‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶ñ‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßã‡ßü‡¶æ‡ßú‡¶ï‡ßá' ‡¶∏‡ßã‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶á‡¶û‡ßç‡¶ú‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶ü‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶®‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Gamification is used to engage employees in security awareness. By turning boring training into a game (like Capture The Flag or simulation rewards), organizations hope to improve "Baseline Hygiene." However, attackers sometimes use gamified lures‚Äîlike fake "spin the wheel" prizes or mobile game mods‚Äîto trick users into installing malware.

---

<a id="H"></a>

## H)

---

<b>Word:</b> Hardening

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb (Gerund)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∂‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßÄ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶¶ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶Ö‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßü‡ßã‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßÄ‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶Ö‡¶Ç‡¶∂‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶¶ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ù‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Strengthening, Reinforcing, Securing, Fortifying.

<b>English Example:</b> "The target's server hardening was a joke; they left the default ports open, so I walked right in through a basic telnet exploit." (‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶Ç (‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ) ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶∞‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶§‡¶æ; ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶´‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ñ‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ñ‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤, ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßú‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> System Hardening is the process of securing a system by reducing its attack surface. This involves removing unnecessary software, disabling unused services/ports, and updating firmware. The goal is to eliminate as many security risks as possible, making it much harder for a hacker to find an entry point.

---

<b>Word:</b> Harvesting

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶π ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶π‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ú‡ßú‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Collecting, Gathering, Scraping, Accumulating.

<b>Example:</b> "My botnet is currently harvesting thousands of emails from that unpatched server; by morning, I‚Äôll have a fresh database to sell on the dark market." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶ü‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶®‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶° ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶á‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶≤ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶π (Harvesting) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá; ‡¶∏‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Harvesting (specifically Credential Harvesting) is the process of using automated tools or social engineering to collect large sets of user data. This is often the second stage of an attack: first, the attacker gains access, then they "harvest" as much sensitive info as possible‚Äîlike usernames, passwords, or PII (Personally Identifiable Information)‚Äîto use or sell later.

---

<b>Word:</b> Hygiene

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ß‡¶ø (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶¶ ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶Ö‡¶≠‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶π)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Maintenance, Sanitation, Cleanliness, Upkeep.

<b>English Example:</b> "Their admin‚Äôs poor password hygiene was my golden ticket; he reused the same trash credentials across ten different servers." (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§‡¶æ (Hygiene) ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶ø; ‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶∂‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶¶‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ú‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Cyber Hygiene refers to the fundamental, routine practices that organizations and individuals perform to maintain system health and improve security. This includes regular patching, using strong/unique passwords, enabling MFA, and deleting unused accounts. Poor hygiene is often the root cause of successful breaches because it leaves simple, preventable vulnerabilities open for exploit.

---

<b>Term:</b> Baseline Hygiene

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶•‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ß‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßÇ‡¶®‡¶§‡¶Æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡ßå‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶™‡¶¶‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶™‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶á ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶â‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶§)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Core security, Fundamental safeguards, Basic security hygiene, Essential maintenance.

<b>English Example:</b> "Their network was a joke; they didn't even have baseline hygiene like disabling guest accounts, so I walked right in through the front door." (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∂‡¶æ ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤; ‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßÇ‡¶®‡¶§‡¶Æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ì (Baseline hygiene) ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶®‡¶æ, ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶¶‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶ú‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßú‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Baseline Hygiene represents the "bare minimum" security controls an organization must implement to defend against low-level, automated threats. This typically includes basic steps like keeping software updated, using firewalls, and enforcing strong password policies. Without this baseline, a system is vulnerable to even the most unsophisticated "script kiddie" attacks.

---

<a id="I"></a>

## I)

---

<b>Word:</b> Imitating

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Present Participle)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Mimicking, Copying, Emulating, Impersonating.

<b>Example:</b> "The hacker is imitating the voice of the bank manager using AI to trick the staff into resetting the master password." (‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶Ü‡¶á (AI) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ç‡¶ï ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶£‡ßç‡¶†‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ (Imitating) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡ßÄ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ß‡ßã‡¶Å‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, imitating is a key step in Impersonation attacks. This can be digital‚Äîsuch as a website imitating a bank's UI‚Äîor behavioral, where an attacker learns the specific vocabulary and writing style of a CEO to make a phishing email seem more authentic. Modern tools like Deepfakes have made imitating audio and video nearly perfect, increasing the risk of successful social engineering.

---

<b>Word:</b> Impersonating

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Present Participle)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶õ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂ ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßü ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ

<b>Synonyms:</b> Masquerading, Posing as, Mimicking, Imitating.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôm impersonating the IT support lead on this call; the panicked employee is giving me their remote access codes without asking a single question." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶ï‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶õ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂ ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ (Impersonating) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶Ü‡¶§‡¶ô‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶® ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶°‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Impersonating is a core tactic in Social Engineering. It involves a threat actor pretending to be a trusted figure‚Äîlike a CEO, a technician, or a government official‚Äîto manipulate victims into performing actions or divulging confidential information. This can happen over the phone (Vishing), via email, or even in person.

---

<b>Word:</b> Inference

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶π‡¶£ (‡¶â‡¶™‡¶≤‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶ß ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶â‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ø‡ßå‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßå‡¶Å‡¶õ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Deduction, Conclusion, Reasoning, Assumption.

<b>English Example:</b> "I don't need your cleartext files; by simple inference from your traffic patterns, I already know when you're moving the money and where it's going." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ü ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßü‡ßã‡¶ú‡¶® ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶á; ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶® ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø ‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶•‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, an Inference Attack occurs when an attacker deduces sensitive information by observing non-sensitive data or patterns. For example, by analyzing the timing or size of encrypted packets, a hacker can infer the type of activity a user is performing without ever breaking the encryption itself.

---

<b>Word:</b> Intel (Slang for Intelligence)

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ó‡ßã‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ó‡ßã‡¶™‡¶® ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶¶ (‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶π ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Intelligence, Information, Recon, Data.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôve gathered enough intel on their network topology; now I know exactly which outdated server to hit for the initial breach." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶ü‡¶™‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶ú‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡¶•‡ßá‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ó‡ßã‡¶™‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø (Intel) ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶π ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶•‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶® ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶ò‡¶æ‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, "Intel" usually refers to Cyber Threat Intelligence (CTI). It is the information used by organizations to understand the threats that have, will, or are currently targeting them. Conversely, hackers gather "recon intel" to identify vulnerabilities, employee habits, and software versions before launching an attack.

---

<b>Word:</b> Interacting

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Present Participle)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶•‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Communicating, Engaging, Connecting, Interfacing.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôm currently interacting with their SQL database through an unsanitized input field; a few more queries and I'll have the full admin table dumped." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶∏‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶è‡¶≤ (SQL) ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶®‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ú‡¶° ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶ü ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó (Interacting) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶Ü‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶® ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶¨‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, "interacting" often refers to how an attacker or a script communicates with a target system. This could be interacting with a compromised shell, an API, or a database. Monitoring how users are interacting with a network is a key part of User and Entity Behavior Analytics (UEBA) to spot hijacked accounts.

---

<b>Word:</b> Intimidation

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶≠‡ßÄ‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¶‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∂‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡ßü ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã (‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶≠‡ßü ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Coercion, Terrorizing, Bullying, Pressure.

<b>Example:</b> "The hacker used intimidation, threatening to leak private photos unless the victim paid the ransom within an hour." (‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶≠‡ßÄ‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¶‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∂‡¶® (Intimidation) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤, ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶ò‡¶£‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶™‡¶£ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶§ ‡¶õ‡¶¨‡¶ø ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Intimidation is a powerful tool in social engineering and extortion (like Ransomware or Sextortion). Attackers often assume a position of authority‚Äîlike a police officer or a tax official‚Äîand use aggressive language to frighten the victim. The goal is to bypass the victim's logical thinking by triggering a "fight or flight" emotional response, making them more likely to comply with the attacker's demands.

---

<b>Word:</b> Invoice

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶≠‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≤ (‡¶™‡¶£‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Ö‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶• ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ß ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶ú ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Bill, Statement, Payment request, Receipt.

<b>Example:</b> "I just sent a spoofed invoice to the HR department with a macro-laden attachment; one click to 'view the bill' and I'm inside their network." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶á‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶á‡¶ö‡¶Ü‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ï ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤‡¶∏‡¶π ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶≠‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∏ (Invoice) ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; '‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶®' ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶¨‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, an Invoice is one of the most common "Lures" used in phishing and Business Email Compromise (BEC) attacks. Because employees handle invoices daily, they are more likely to open a malicious PDF or Doc file disguised as a bill, allowing attackers to deploy malware or steal wire transfers.

---

## J)

---

<a id="K"></a>

## K)

---

<b>Word:</b> Kernel

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡¶ú‡ßç‡¶ú‡¶æ (‡¶Ö‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶Ö‡¶Ç‡¶∂ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶ü‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Core, Central part, Nucleus, Root.

<b>English Example:</b> "Once I've injected my rootkit into the kernel, I own the entire OS; no antivirus will ever see me because I‚Äôm operating at a level deeper than their scanners." (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶®‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ (Kernel) ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨, ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡¶ñ‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶¨‡ßá; ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ì ‡¶ó‡¶≠‡ßÄ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> The Kernel is the heart of an Operating System (OS). It manages the communication between the computer's hardware (CPU, memory, devices) and its software. In cybersecurity, a Kernel-level exploit is extremely dangerous because it gives the attacker total control over the system, allowing them to hide their tracks from security software that runs at a higher "User" level.

---

<a id="L"></a>

## L)

---

<b>Word:</b> Laterally

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adverb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∂‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶Ü‡ßú‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶á ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶õ‡ßú‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßú‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Sideways, Across, Inter-network.

<b>English Example:</b> "Once I gained a foothold on the receptionist's PC, I moved laterally through the network until I found the domain controller." (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶™‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞, ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∂‡¶ø (Laterally) ‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶≠ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶§‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶°‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Lateral Movement refers to the techniques cyber-attackers use to move progressively through a network as they search for key assets and data. After gaining initial access to a single endpoint, the attacker spreads "laterally" to other systems to escalate privileges and find the ultimate target.

---

<b>Word:</b> Legitimate

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡ßà‡¶ß ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤ (‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶Æ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡ßÄ ‡¶∏‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶®‡ßü)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Authentic, Genuine, Authorized, Real.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôve injected my malicious script into a legitimate system process, so the antivirus thinks everything is normal while I siphon off the data." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßà‡¶ß (Legitimate) ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø, ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶∏‡¶¨‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, the goal of an attacker is often to appear legitimate. This is seen in Living off the Land (LotL) attacks, where hackers use legitimate administrative tools (like PowerShell or WMI) to perform malicious activities. Because the tools are trusted by the OS, they are less likely to trigger security alerts compared to custom malware.

---

<b>Word:</b> Listicles

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun (Plural)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ-‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ß (‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá; ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶á ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶õ‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> List-articles, Bulleted features, Ranked lists.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "I‚Äôm hosting a few clickbait listicles like 'Top 10 Privacy Tools'; once they download the 'recommended' software, my hidden miner starts running in the background."
