(‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø '‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡ßß‡ß¶‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßÄ ‡¶ü‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡¶∏' ‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶á‡¶ü ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤ (Listicles) ‡¶π‡ßã‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶â ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ '‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶∂ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ' ‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶° ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá, ‡¶Ö‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶ø‡¶°‡ßá‡¶® ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In the world of cybercrime, Listicles are frequently used as "clickbait" in social engineering campaigns. Because they are easy to read and highly shareable, attackers use them to draw traffic to malicious websites or to trick users into downloading compromised software disguised as helpful tools listed in the article.

---

<b>Word:</b> Lure

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶ß ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶¶‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶≠‡¶® ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã

<b>Synonyms:</b> Entice, Attract, Seduce, Decoy.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôll lure the target to my malicious site with a fake 'Security Alert' email; once they click, the browser exploit will do the rest of the dirty work." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡ßü‡¶æ '‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü' ‡¶á‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶ß (Lure) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßã; ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶Ç‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶ü‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßÅ ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, a lure is the specific content used in a social engineering attack to convince a victim to take an action. While "bait" is often a physical or digital object, a lure is usually the psychological hook‚Äîlike a sense of urgency, fear, or a too-good-to-be-true offer‚Äîthat drives the success of a phishing campaign.

---

<b>Term:</b> Novel Lures

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶≠‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶¶ (‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶®‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶∏‡¶¨ ‡¶ï‡ßå‡¶∂‡¶≤ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶ß ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡ßü)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Original baits, Unique traps, Fresh deceptions, New-age phishing tactics.

<b>Example:</b> "Hackers are using novel lures related to the latest global events to trick people into clicking malicious links." (‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∑‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ô‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶ß ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶¨‡ßà‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ò‡¶ü‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶≠‡¶® (Novel lures) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, a Lure is the "hook" used in a phishing attack to grab a victim's attention. When we call them Novel, it means they are creative and exploit current trends or psychological triggers that people haven't been warned about yet. For example, during a major sporting event or a health crisis, attackers create novel lures like "Click here for free tickets" or "Download the emergency guide." Because the lures are new, they often bypass email filters that are looking for older, known patterns.

---

<a id="M"></a>

## M)

---

<b>Word:</b> Macros

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun (Plural)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶∏ (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶®‡ßç‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá, ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Automated scripts, Embedded commands, Mini-programs.

<b>Example:</b> "I sent them a fake invoice with malicious macros hidden inside; once that clueless accountant clicks 'Enable Content,' my shell script will execute and give me full remote access." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶≠‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ï ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶∏ (Macros) ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ü‡¶õ‡ßá; ‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ß ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶®‡¶á 'Enable Content'-‡¶è ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá, ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶≤ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßÅ ‡¶π‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Macros are small scripts used to automate repetitive tasks in Microsoft Office documents. Attackers use "Macro-based Malware" to deliver payloads. Since macros can run system-level commands, keeping them disabled by default is a critical security practice to prevent automated infection upon opening a file.

---

<b>Word:</b> Microtasks

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun (Plural)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ö‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßÅ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßú ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßü)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Small units of work, Granular tasks, Sub-tasks, Mini-jobs.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôve split the botnet deployment into microtasks across thousands of zombie nodes so no single machine triggers a CPU usage alarm." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶ü‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßü‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶ø ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡ßá (Microtasks) ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶® CPU ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, microtasks are used in <b>Distributed Computing</b> attacks. By breaking a massive job (like cracking a complex hash) into millions of microtasks, an attacker can use a distributed network of compromised devices to perform the work in parallel, making the operation faster and harder to detect by traditional security monitors.

---

<b>Word:</b> Mimicked

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Past Tense / Past Participle)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶π‡ßÅ‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÅ ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶â‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Imitated, Copied, Spoofed, Simulated.

<b>Example:</b> "I mimicked the company‚Äôs internal update server so perfectly that their workstations downloaded my virus without a single warning." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶Ü‡¶™‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶§ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶§‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶≤ (Mimicked) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶õ‡¶æ‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶° ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, mimicking is the foundation of Spoofing and Impersonation attacks. Attackers mimic legitimate login screens, email addresses, or even network protocols to bypass human and technical defenses. This exploit relies on the victim's trust in a familiar interface or brand to execute unauthorized commands.

---

<b>Word:</b> Minion

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ü‡¶ú‡ßç‡¶û‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶π ‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßÄ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶∏ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶≠ ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∏ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Zombie, Slave, Bot, Puppet, Subordinate.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôve infected over five thousand IoT devices; each minion is now waiting for my command to unleash a massive traffic surge on the target's portal." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶ö ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞‡¶ì ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶ì‡¶ü‡¶ø (IoT) ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∏ ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶´‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßÄ ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∏ (Minion) ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶™‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶Ü‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ú‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In a botnet architecture, a Minion (or Bot/Zombie) is a compromised computer or device that is controlled remotely by a "Botmaster." These devices are used collectively to perform large-scale attacks, such as DDoS or mass spamming, often without the owners' knowledge.

---

<b>Word:</b> Monetize

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶®‡¶ó‡¶¶‡ßÄ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶â‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã (‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶®‡¶æ)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Cash in, Capitalize, Liquidate, Profit from.

<b>Example:</b> "Stealing the data was the easy part; now I need to monetize these credit card dumps on the underground market before the banks flag them as stolen." (‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶ú ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶Ü‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ó‡¶¶‡ßÄ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ (Monetize) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá, ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶π‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶π‡ßç‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶á‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In the cybercrime ecosystem, Monetization is the final stage of an attack. It involves turning stolen assets‚Äî‡πÄ‡∏ä‡πà‡∏ô personal info, corporate secrets, or computing power‚Äîinto profit. This can be done through ransomware ransoms, selling data on dark web forums, or using compromised systems for cryptojacking.

---

<a id="N"></a>

## N)

---

<b>Word:</b> Novelty

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßç‡¶¨ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶¨‡¶§‡ßç‡¶¨ (‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶®‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡ßÇ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£ ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶®)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Originality, Newness, Innovation, Uniqueness.

<b>English Example:</b> "The novelty of this polymorphic engine is that it changes its signature every time it spreads, making it invisible to traditional antivirus scanners." (‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶™‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶∞‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶á‡¶û‡ßç‡¶ú‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßç‡¶¨ (Novelty) ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶§‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶õ‡ßú‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶§‡¶§‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶´‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, <b>Novelty</b> is a major challenge for defenders. Novel Attacks (like Zero-days) are dangerous because there are no pre-existing signatures or rules to stop them. Security systems that rely on "Heuristics" or AI try to identify this novelty by looking for unusual behavior rather than matching known patterns.

---

<a id="O"></a>

## O)

---

<b>Word:</b> Obsession

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ü‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ò‡ßã‡¶∞ (‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶§‡ßÄ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶•‡¶æ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶®‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Fixation, Passion, Infatuation, Compulsion.

<b>English Example:</b> "My obsession with their root directory won't end until I find the hidden private keys and drain every bit of data they have." (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§‡¶æ (Obsession) ‡¶§‡¶§‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ, ‡¶Ø‡¶§‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡ßÄ-‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, an obsession often describes the mindset of a persistent threat actor or a dedicated researcher. This "hacker mindset" involves deep focus on a single target or vulnerability for extended periods. In defense, it can refer to Hyper-vigilance, where security teams are obsessed with monitoring every single packet to ensure zero breaches.

---

<b>Word:</b> Opportunistic

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßÄ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡¶∏‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÄ (‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßü, ‡¶¨‡¶∞‡¶Ç ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶á ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Shrewd, Tactical, Exploitative, Advantageous.

<b>English Example:</b> "I didn't target your company specifically; I just ran an opportunistic scan for unpatched RDP ports and you happened to leave the door wide open." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø; ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶ß‡ßÅ ‡¶Ü‡¶®‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶° RDP ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßÄ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶Ü‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡¶¨‡¶∂‡¶§ ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶ñ‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ñ‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, an Opportunistic Attack is not targeted at a specific person or organization. Instead, the attacker looks for any system with a known vulnerability (like an old software version or weak password). It‚Äôs like a thief walking through a parking lot checking for unlocked car doors‚Äîthey don't care whose car it is, they just want an easy entry.

---

<a id="P"></a>

## P)

---

<b>Word:</b> Paved

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective / Verb (Past Tense)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶ó‡¶Æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶• ‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡ßü)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Prepared, Facilitated, Cleared, Established.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "The intern's weak password paved the way for my lateral movement across the entire corporate network." (‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶®‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßá ‡¶ò‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßá‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶• ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶ó‡¶Æ (Paved) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In a security context, paved often describes how a vulnerability or human error creates an easy path for an attacker. Conversely, "The Paved Road" is a defensive concept where security teams provide developers with pre-approved, secure tools and infrastructures to ensure that the easiest way to build something is also the most secure way.

---

<b>Word:</b> Phreaking

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶Æ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶´‡ßã‡¶® ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡¶§ ‡¶´‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø-‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Phone hacking, Telecom hacking, Blue boxing.

<b>Example:</b> "In the early days of hacking, phreaking was popular for bypassing long-distance call charges using special frequency tones." (‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶´‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶® ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßÇ‡¶∞‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ú ‡¶è‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø '‡¶´‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶Ç' (Phreaking) ‡¶Ö‡¶§‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Phreaking is a "vintage" hacking term that combines the words "phone" and "freak." It refers to the study and manipulation of telephone systems. The most famous example is the use of a Blue Box, a device that mimicked the 2600Hz tone used by internal telephone switches to authorize long-distance calls for free. While modern digital networks have made traditional phreaking nearly impossible, it paved the way for modern computer hacking.

---

<b>Word:</b> Phishing Kits

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun (Plural)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶∏ (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶ú ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶¨ ‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶≤ ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶á‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Phish kits, Scam toolkits, Attack packages, Fake-site templates.

<b>Example:</b> "I don't need to build a fake bank page from scratch; I just bought a premium phishing kit that looks identical to the original and even bypasses basic 2FA." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ç‡¶ï ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶ú ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶á; ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶ß‡ßÅ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶ü (Phishing kit) ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶¶‡¶Æ ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ 2FA-‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶ì ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> A Phishing Kit is a pre-packaged collection of tools (HTML pages, PHP scripts, images) that allows even unskilled "script kiddies" to launch sophisticated phishing attacks. These kits are often sold on the dark web and come with easy-to-use dashboards to collect stolen credentials in real-time.

---

<b>Word:</b> Pivot

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb / Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßå‡¶∂‡¶≤ (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶•‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Lateral movement, Relay, Tunneling, Leapfrog.

<b>English Example:</b> "Gaining access to that low-level employee's laptop was just the start; now I‚Äôll pivot through the internal network until I reach the domain controller." (‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡ßÄ‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶ü‡¶™‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶≤ ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶¨ (Pivot) ‡¶Ø‡¶§‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶°‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßå‡¶Å‡¶õ‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Pivoting is a technique used by attackers to use a compromised system as a "stepping stone" to attack other systems in the same network that are not directly accessible from the internet. It is the core of "Lateral Movement," allowing hackers to bypass firewalls by moving from the inside.

---

<b>Word:</b> Plausible

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶¶‡ßÉ‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶§‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶π‡ßü ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡¶§ ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ó‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶™ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡ßü ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ß‡ßã‡¶Å‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶•‡ßá‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶¨‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶§)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Believable, Credible, Reasonable, Likely.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "The phishing email needs a plausible excuse, like a 'failed login attempt' from a foreign IP, to scare the target into handing over their credentials immediately." (‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶≠‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶°‡ßá‡¶®‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶á‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶Ø (Plausible) ‡¶Ö‡¶ú‡ßÅ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§ ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞, ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶®‚Äî‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶™‡¶ø ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá '‡¶≤‡¶ó‡¶á‡¶® ‡¶ö‡ßá‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶•‡¶§‡¶æ'‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Plausibility is the backbone of Social Engineering. Attacks like Business Email Compromise (BEC) succeed because the attacker‚Äôs story is plausible‚Äîusing correct corporate jargon, realistic-looking email templates, or timing the attack with real-world events. If an attack isn't plausible, it is easily flagged as suspicious by the user or security filters.

---

<b>Word:</b> Plausible Deniability

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡ßÄ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶§‡¶æ (‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶ø‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßà‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡ßà‡¶ß ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶ú‡ßú‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶®‡¶æ, ‡¶´‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡ßÄ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶¨ ‡¶π‡ßü)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Reasonable doubt, Cover story, Defensive masking, Strategic ambiguity.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "I‚Äôve set up the malware to self-destruct and wipe all logs after the heist; even if they catch the packet flow, I have plausible deniability because the traffic looks like it's coming from a compromised IoT toaster." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶Ç‡¶∏ ‡¶π‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶∏‡¶¨ ‡¶≤‡¶ó ‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá; ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶¶‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶´‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ì ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá, ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶¨‡ßÄ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶§‡¶æ (Plausible deniability) ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶π‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ IoT ‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Plausible Deniability often refers to a situation where an individual can deny knowledge of or responsibility for a particular action because there is no evidence to prove otherwise. Technically, it is seen in hidden volumes in disk encryption (where a user can claim a hidden partition doesn't exist) or in anti-forensics, where attackers hide their tracks so well that it's impossible to legally or technically link the attack to them.

---

<b>Word:</b> Pomodoro

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßã‡¶°‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßã (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡ß®‡ß´ ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡ß´ ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßü)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Time-boxing, Interval timing, Focus sessions.

<b>English Example:</b> "I set a Pomodoro timer to stay focused; twenty-five minutes of intense brute-forcing, then five minutes to clean my tracks before the next cycle." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶´‡ßã‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßã‡¶°‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶™‡¶Å‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶∂ ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶∏ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü-‡¶´‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡¶¨‡ßá, ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÄ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶π‡ßç‡¶® ‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶ö ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> While originally a productivity technique, in cybersecurity, "Pomodoro" or interval-based work is used by researchers to prevent burnout during deep-focus tasks like vulnerability research or log analysis. It ensures the analyst remains sharp enough to spot subtle anomalies in massive datasets.

---

<b>Word:</b> Procrastination

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¶‡ßÄ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ò‡¶∏‡ßÇ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡¶æ (‡¶Ö‡¶≤‡¶∏‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ú‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Delay, Postponement, Dilly-dallying, Hesitation.

<b>English Example:</b> "Their admin‚Äôs procrastination in patching that old vulnerability was my golden ticket; I stayed inside their network for months because they kept 'forgetting' to update the server." (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßÄ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ò‡¶∏‡ßÇ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ (Procrastination) ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£ ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó; ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶™‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá '‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßá' ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, procrastination is a major risk factor. When organizations delay critical security updates (Patch Management), they leave a "window of vulnerability" open. Hackers rely on this human tendency to ignore or delay boring maintenance tasks to exploit well-known flaws that should have been fixed long ago.

---

<b>Word:</b> Prominence

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø, ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶§‡ßç‡¶¨ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡ßÉ‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶§‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶•‡¶æ‡ßü, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶®‡¶ú‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Importance, Notoriety, Visibility, Fame.

<b>Example:</b> "I don‚Äôt care about the money; I‚Äôm defacing their homepage to gain prominence in the underground hacking scene and prove no one is safe." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡ßã‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶æ; ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶ú‡¶ó‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø (Prominence) ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶â ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶¶ ‡¶®‡ßü ‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶ú‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Prominence often relates to the "attack surface" or the visibility of a target. High-profile organizations have more digital prominence, making them "lucrative targets" for APTs (Advanced Persistent Threats) and hacktivists. From a defensive side, reducing the prominence of sensitive internal assets‚Äîby hiding them behind VPNs or non-standard ports‚Äîis a key part of risk mitigation.

---

<b>Word:</b> Proxies

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun (Plural)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ß‡¶ø (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÄ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßü ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶™‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Intermediaries, Relays, Gateways, Anonymizers.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôm routing my attack through a chain of residential proxies across three different continents; by the time they trace the IP, I‚Äôll be long gone with their data." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶® ‡¶Æ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ø (Proxies) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶™‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶¶‡ßÇ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶¨‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Proxies act as a bridge between a user and the internet. While businesses use them for filtering and caching, hackers use them to mask their origin and bypass geo-blocking. A "Proxy Chain" makes it extremely difficult for investigators to find the attacker's actual physical location.

---

<b>Word:</b> Privilege

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶Æ‡¶§‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶â‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶ö‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∏)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Authority, Access rights, Permission, Entitlement.

<b>Example:</b> "I started with a low-level guest account, but after a quick exploit, I‚Äôve gained root privilege; now I can wipe their entire server with a single command." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶Æ, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ú (‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞) ‡¶™‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Privilege refers to the level of access a user has. "Privilege Escalation" is a common attack where a hacker moves from a standard user to an administrative level (like 'root' or 'admin') to gain full control over a system.

---

<b>Word:</b> Psychological

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï (‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶§)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Mental, Cognitive, Emotional, Behavioral.

<b>Example:</b> "Social engineering isn't about hacking the computer; it‚Äôs about hacking the human by using psychological pressure like urgency or fear." (‡¶∏‡ßã‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶á‡¶û‡ßç‡¶ú‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∑‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶®‡¶Ø‡¶º; ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶π‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ú‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï (Psychological) ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶™ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßü‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∑‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Psychological Manipulation is the core of Social Engineering. Attackers exploit human nature‚Äîsuch as trust, curiosity, or the desire to be helpful‚Äîto bypass technical defenses. By creating a psychological trigger (e.g., an email saying "Your account will be deleted in 1 hour"), they force victims to act impulsively without verifying the source.

---

<a id="Q"></a>

## Q)

---

<b>Word:</b> Quarterly

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective / Adverb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßà‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶® ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Every three months, Once a quarter, Periodical.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôve timed my ransomware to trigger right before their quarterly financial report; they‚Äôll pay anything to avoid showing a zeroed-out balance to their shareholders." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∞‚Äç‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶Æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßà‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ü‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶•‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶ö‡¶≤ ‡¶π‡ßü; ‡¶∂‡ßá‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶π‡ßã‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶∂‡ßÇ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶∏ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶è‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶ø ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity compliance (like PCI-DSS or SOC2), quarterly audits and vulnerability scans are mandatory. Attackers often exploit the gaps between these scheduled checks, knowing that security posture might weaken between one quarter's audit and the next.

---

<a id="R"></a>

## R)

---

<b>Word:</b> Reciprocity

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶®‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶®-‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶® (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡ßå‡¶∂‡¶≤ ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßú ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßü)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Mutual exchange, Give-and-take, Interdependence, Correlation.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "I used the principle of reciprocity by sending the admin a 'free' helpful script; now he feels obligated to answer my questions about the server's internal architecture." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø (Reciprocity) ‡¶®‡ßÄ‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø '‡¶´‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø' ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶Ü‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶ï‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶â‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßà‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ß ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Reciprocity is a key psychological trigger used in Social Engineering. Humans have a natural tendency to want to repay a favor. Attackers exploit this by providing a small gift, a compliment, or a helpful tip to a victim, creating a sense of indebtedness. This makes the victim more likely to comply with a later request, such as sharing sensitive information or clicking a malicious link.

---

<b>Word:</b> Roll (Slang/Informal)

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Ø‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßÄ ‡¶¨‡¶¶‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Rotate, Cycle, Reset, Refresh.

<b>English Example:</b> "If the sysadmin doesn't roll those SSH keys within the hour, my backdoor will stay wide open for the final payload." (‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶® ‡¶Ø‡¶¶‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶ò‡¶£‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶ì‡¶á SSH ‡¶ï‡ßÄ‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶® (Roll) ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá, ‡¶§‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶°‡ßã‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶° ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶á ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In security protocols, "rolling" refers to Credential Rotation. It is a defensive practice where passwords, API keys, or encryption certificates are updated regularly. This limits the "window of opportunity" for a hacker; even if a key is stolen, it becomes useless once the system rolls it to a new one.

---

<b>Word:</b> Roll (List/Record)

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶æ (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßü)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Register, Roster, Catalog, Directory.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôve breached the payroll roll; now I‚Äôm editing the salaries to redirect the cash flow into my offshore accounts." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßá-‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶≤ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶ø (Roll) ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶§‡¶®‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶´‡¶∂‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In a technical context, a roll (or roster) is a structured record of entities. Cybercriminals often target a "User Roll" or "System Directory" to identify high-privilege targets within an organization. Gaining access to these records allows an attacker to map out the entire network hierarchy before launching a targeted strike.

---

<b>Word:</b> Rolling

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Continuous) / Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶§ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶®‡¶∂‡ßÄ‡¶≤.

<b>Synonyms:</b> Ongoing, Continuous, Rotating, Sequential.

<b>Example:</b> "I‚Äôm using a rolling proxy to mask my IP address every ten seconds, making it impossible for their firewall to pin me down." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶™‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¶‡¶∂ ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶®‡¶∂‡ßÄ‡¶≤ (Rolling) ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶´‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶¨ ‡¶π‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßú‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Rolling often refers to Rolling Codes (used in car key fobs to prevent replay attacks) or Rolling Updates. From an offensive perspective, a "rolling attack" involves constantly changing parameters‚Äîlike IP addresses or file signatures‚Äîto evade detection by security software that looks for static patterns.

---

<b>Word:</b> Rolling in

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Phrasal Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶£‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶¨ ‡¶∏‡¶π‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Pouring in, Flooding in, Accumulating, Streaming in.

<b>Example:</b> "Once the ransomware hit their servers, the Bitcoin payments started rolling in faster than their IT team could scream for help." (‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶∞‚Äç‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶ò‡¶æ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶≤‡ßã, ‡¶§‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡ßé‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ì ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶§ ‡¶ó‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ï‡ßü‡ßá‡¶® ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶§‡ßá (Rolling in) ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßã‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In the context of cybercrime, rolling in often describes the influx of data or profit during the "Monetization" phase of an attack. Whether it‚Äôs stolen credit card numbers from a skimmer or crypto-ransom payments, it signifies a successful breach where the attacker is reaping the rewards of their exploit in high volume.

---

<b>Word:</b> Rootkit

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶ü (‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ó‡ßã‡¶™‡¶® ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶¶‡¶Æ ‡¶ó‡¶≠‡ßÄ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßÇ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶£ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡ßü ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶®‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Stealth malware, Kernel-level exploit, Deep persistence tool.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôve successfully injected a rootkit into their OS kernel; even if they reinstall the apps, I'll still be ghosting their system from the shadows." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡¶è‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶®‡ßá‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶≤‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶¶‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶∞‡¶ø-‡¶á‡¶®‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶≤‡¶ì ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá, ‡¶§‡¶¨‡ßÅ‡¶ì ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡¶¨‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> A Rootkit is a collection of software tools that enables an unauthorized user to gain control of a computer system without being detected. Because it often resides at the kernel level (the core of the OS), it can hide its files, processes, and network connections from standard security tools. Removing a rootkit is extremely difficult and often requires a complete hardware wipe or specialized low-level scanning.

---

<a id="S"></a>

## S)

---

<b>Word:</b> Sanely

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adverb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶• ‡¶Æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßÅ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá (‡¶Ø‡ßå‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Rationally, Sensibly, Logically, Wisely.

<b>English Example:</b> "No admin can sanely argue that leaving a root password as 'admin123' is a minor risk after I‚Äôve just emptied their vault." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶á ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶• ‡¶Æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá (Sanely) ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶Ø‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡ßá, ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° 'admin123' ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶ü‡ßã ‡¶ù‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, acting "sanely" refers to following Best Practices and rational risk management. A system is considered "sanely configured" when it follows the Principle of Least Privilege (PoLP) and logical security controls that any reasonable professional would implement to prevent predictable attacks.

---

<b>Word:</b> Severe

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶π (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ù‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Critical, Extreme, Acute, Intense.

<b>English Example:</b> "The vulnerability I found is classified as severe; one click and I get a remote shell with root privileges, bypassing every firewall they have." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶π‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶§‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶§‡¶∞ (Severe); ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ú‡¶∏‡¶π ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶¨, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶´‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, "Severe" is often used to describe the severity level of a vulnerability (like in the CVSS scale). A severe rating means the flaw is easily exploitable and could result in a total system compromise, data loss, or complete loss of service, requiring immediate patching.

---

<b>Word:</b> Siphon

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ß‡ßÄ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ß‡ßÄ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ó‡ßã‡¶™‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡ßà‡¶ß‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Drain, Bleed, Extract, Funnel.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "My script is designed to siphon a few cents from every transaction; by morning, I‚Äôll have millions sitting in my offshore wallet without triggering any alarms." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶®‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶® ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ó‡ßã‡¶™‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ (Siphon) ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø; ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶∏‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶´‡¶∂‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶ñ ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶ñ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶ú‡¶Æ‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, to siphon means to slowly and stealthily extract data or funds over a period of time to avoid detection by threshold-based monitoring systems. Unlike a sudden "bulk dump," siphoning is a low-and-slow technique often used in financial fraud or long-term data exfiltration (APT attacks).

---

<b>Word:</b> Siphon off

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Phrasal Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶¨‡ßú ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶â‡ßé‡¶∏ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßå‡¶∂‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡¶Ç‡¶∂‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶¶ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶æ)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Divert, Embezzle, Filch, Draw off.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "While their IT team was busy fighting the DDoS, I managed to siphon off the encrypted customer database through a hidden tunnel." (‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶°‡ßã‡¶∏ ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶†‡ßá‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤, ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶π‡¶ø‡¶°‡ßá‡¶® ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶≤ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∏‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá (Siphon off) ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Siphon off is a term used to describe the illicit diversion of funds or data. In a cyber-heist, an attacker might "siphon off" small amounts of money from thousands of accounts to stay under the radar of fraud detection systems, or slowly exfiltrate sensitive files during a prolonged breach.

---

<b>Word:</b> Skim

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶§ ‡¶ö‡ßã‡¶ñ ‡¶¨‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã (‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ) ‡¶Ö‡¶•‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Glance, Scan, Browse (General); Data theft, Sniff (Technical).

<b>Example:</b> "I installed a tiny device on the ATM to skim the credit card data from every customer who uses it today." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶è‡¶Æ ‡¶¨‡ßÅ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∏ ‡¶¨‡¶∏‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶ú ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø (Skim) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Skimming refers to a specific type of physical identity theft. Attackers place a "skimmer" (a small, camouflaged device) over a legitimate card slot (like at an ATM or gas pump). As you slide your card, the device skims the information from the magnetic stripe. This is often combined with a tiny hidden camera to record your PIN.

---

<b>Word:</b> Sophistication

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ú‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§ ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶õ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ ‡¶â‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶ö‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶¶‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßå‡¶∂‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶Ø‡¶º)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Complexity, Advancement, Refinement, Expertise.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "The sheer sophistication of this rootkit suggests it wasn't made by a script kiddie; this is state-sponsored craftsmanship designed to stay hidden for years." (‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡¶∞‡¶Æ ‡¶ú‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§ ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£ (Sophistication) ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡ßá ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ù‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶®‡ßü; ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶Æ‡¶¶‡¶¶‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶∞‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶õ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶õ‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Sophistication refers to the level of technical skill and resources behind an attack. A "High-Sophistication" attack (like an APT) often involves custom-built malware, zero-day exploits, and multi-stage evasion techniques. Security analysts measure sophistication to determine if they are facing a random attacker or a highly organized group.

---

<b>Word:</b> Spamming

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Gerund)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶Ö‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∑‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶â‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶π‡ßÄ‡¶®‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ú ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Mass-mailing, Flooding, Junking, Bulk messaging.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôm spamming their corporate inboxes with a fresh batch of macro-enabled invoices; out of five thousand employees, someone is bound to be stupid enough to click." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶¨‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã-‡¶è‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡¶° ‡¶á‡¶®‡¶≠‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶Ç (Spamming) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶ö ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶â ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶â ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶á ‡¶Ø‡¶•‡ßá‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡ßã‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ô‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, spamming is often the delivery mechanism for phishing or malware. While most spam is just annoying advertising, "Malicious Spam" (Malspam) is used to distribute trojans, ransomware, or credential-harvesting links to a massive number of users simultaneously to increase the odds of a successful infection.

---

<b>Word:</b> Spear

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb (Used as an adjective in cybersecurity)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£ (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶®: ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ç)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Targeted, Focused, Precise, Pointed.

<b>Example:</b> "I'm not sending a million spam emails; I'm launching a spear attack against the head of security to get his admin credentials." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑ ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶á‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶æ; ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶π‡ßá‡¶° ‡¶Ö‡¶´ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶°‡ßá‡¶®‡¶∂‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞ (Spear) ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Spear is most commonly associated with Spear Phishing. Unlike standard phishing which is sent to thousands of random people, spear phishing is a highly targeted attack directed at a specific individual or organization. The attacker researches the victim's name, job title, and colleagues to make the email seem incredibly authentic, increasing the success rate significantly.

---

<b>Word:</b> Spikes

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun (Plural) / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶π‡¶†‡¶æ‡ßé ‡¶¨‡ßÉ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶â‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶ó‡¶§‡¶ø (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Surges, Peaks, Sharp increases, Escalations.

<b>Example:</b> "As soon as I launched the DDoS attack, I saw the traffic spikes redline on their server monitors, right before the whole system crashed." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶ì‡¶è‡¶∏ (DDoS) ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßÅ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡ßÉ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ø (Spikes) ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶Æ, ‡¶Ü‡¶∞ ‡¶†‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∂ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, spikes often refer to sudden, abnormal increases in network traffic or CPU usage. Analyzing these spikes is crucial for SOC (Security Operations Center) analysts to detect ongoing attacks like Brute-force, DDoS, or unauthorized data transfers.

---

<b>Term:</b> Quarterly Spikes

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßà‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡ßÉ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ø (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶® ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßú ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶®)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Seasonal surges, Three-month peaks, Cyclical bursts.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôve been tracking their logs for months; those quarterly spikes in financial reporting traffic are the perfect cover for me to slip in and exfiltrate the encrypted ledgers." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡¶ó ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶Ü‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶•‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßü ‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßà‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶¨‡ßÉ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶ø (Quarterly spikes) ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶¶‡¶Æ ‡¶â‡¶™‡¶Ø‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶∏‡ßÅ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶° ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In security monitoring, quarterly spikes are predictable patterns related to business cycles (like tax season or quarterly earnings). Attackers exploit these high-traffic periods because malicious activity can easily blend in with the massive volume of legitimate requests, making it harder for automated filters to flag anomalies.

---

<b>Word:</b> Spoofing

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶ø (‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßü ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ï‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßü ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≠‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Impersonation, Mimicking, Faking, Masquerading.

<b>Example:</b> "I'm spoofing the company‚Äôs internal IP address so the server trusts my connection and lets me bypass the firewall without a password." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶Ü‡¶á‡¶™‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶°‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∏‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶≤ (Spoofing) ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶° ‡¶õ‡¶æ‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶´‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Spoofing is a technique where an attacker disguises a communication from an unknown source as being from a known, trusted source. This can be applied to IP addresses, email headers, GPS signals, or Caller IDs. The goal is to gain access to a system, steal data, or spread malware by bypassing filters that trust the "spoofed" identity.

---

<b>Word:</b> Strain

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ (‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá) ‡¶Ö‡¶•‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ö‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶™

<b>Synonyms:</b> Variant, Version, Pressure, Stress.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "This new strain of the Trojan is so stealthy that no antivirus can sniff it out before I drain the targets' bank accounts." (‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶ü‡¶ø (Strain) ‡¶è‡¶§‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶ó‡ßã‡¶™‡¶®‡ßÄ‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ô‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, a strain refers to a specific version or mutation of a malware family. Just like biological viruses, hackers modify existing code to create new strains that bypass updated security filters. It can also refer to the heavy load placed on system resources during a cyberattack.

---

<b>Terms:</b> Novel Strain

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun Phrase

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶®‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶Æ)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> New variant, Emerging malware, Zero-day strain, Unique mutation.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "I‚Äôve just released a novel strain of ransomware that uses polymorphic code; the blue team's EDR is completely blind to its signature." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶á‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞ ‡¶∞‚Äç‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ (Novel strain) ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶õ‡ßá‡ßú‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶∞‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶° ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá; ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßÅ-‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ EDR ‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ó‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶•‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> A Novel Strain refers to a newly discovered or developed version of a malware family. These are particularly dangerous because security tools (like Antivirus or EDR) often rely on a database of known threats. Since a novel strain has a unique code structure, it can bypass signature-based detection until it is officially identified and analyzed by researchers.

---

<b>Word:</b> Stream

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶π (‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶® ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶π)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Flow, Sequence, Transmission, Feed.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôve tapped into the raw data stream; now I‚Äôm watching every bit of their unencrypted traffic pass through my terminal in real-time." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∞ ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡ßú‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßá‡¶§‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶≤-‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶ø‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, a Stream often refers to a continuous flow of data. For example, a "Byte Stream" is a sequence of bytes used in communication. In cryptography, a Stream Cipher encrypts digits (typically bytes) one by one. Attackers often target data streams via "Man-in-the-Middle" (MitM) attacks to intercept or inject malicious data into the live transmission.

---

<b>Word:</b> Sugar-coating

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Verb (Gerund) / Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶§‡ßá‡¶§‡ßã ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™ ‡¶ï‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡¶æ (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶â‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßü‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶£‡ßÄ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶â‡¶™‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Glossing over, Whitewashing, Sweetening, Soft-pedaling.

<b>English Example:</b> "There‚Äôs no use sugar-coating it; their security is non-existent, and I‚Äôve already siphoned every bit of their encrypted data while they were busy trusting my 'gift' file." (‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡ßú‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá (Sugar-coating) ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶á; ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶≤‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ‡¶á ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶á, ‡¶Ü‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã '‡¶â‡¶™‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞' ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤, ‡¶§‡¶ñ‡¶®‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶®‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶¨ ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity and social engineering, sugar-coating is used to lower a victim's guard. An attacker might present a malicious file as a "bonus," "free gift," or "security patch." By sugar-coating the true nature of the threat, they exploit human psychology to encourage the victim to bypass their own common sense or security protocols.

---

<b>Word:</b> Stylometric

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ñ‡¶®‡¶∂‡ßà‡¶≤‡ßÄ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ (‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶ï‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∂‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶ß‡¶§‡¶ø)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Linguistic profiling, Authorship attribution, Writing style analysis.

<b>English Example:</b> "Scrub your forum posts carefully; if you don't vary your syntax, a stylometric analysis will link your 'anonymous' leaks straight back to your real identity." (‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶´‡ßã‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßã; ‡¶Ø‡¶¶‡¶ø ‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ó‡¶†‡¶® ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶® ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßã, ‡¶§‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ñ‡¶®‡¶∂‡ßà‡¶≤‡ßÄ ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶£ ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶á '‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßÄ' ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶§‡ßã‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤ ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Stylometry is the study of linguistic style. It is used in threat intelligence to identify hackers by analyzing their unique writing patterns, vocabulary, and grammar. Even if an attacker uses a VPN or Tor, their "fingerprint" in the way they write code or messages can lead to their deanonymization.

---

<b>Word:</b> Suspicion

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∏‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶π ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶∂‡¶Ø‡¶º (‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Doubt, Distrust, Skepticism, Misgiving.

<b>English Example:</b> "I have to keep the data packets small and slow to avoid raising any suspicion from their AI-based traffic monitors." (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶Ü‡¶á-‡¶≠‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶∞‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶π (Suspicion) ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶è‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶õ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶ß‡ßÄ‡¶∞‡¶ó‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, "raising suspicion" refers to triggering alerts in security systems like IDS (Intrusion Detection Systems) or SIEM. Attackers use "Low and Slow" tactics or "Living off the Land" (using legitimate system tools) to perform their activities without creating the anomalies that lead to suspicion and discovery.

---

<b>Word:</b> Synthetic

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ï‡ßÉ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶ø‡¶§ (‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßÉ‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶®‡ßü, ‡¶¨‡¶∞‡¶Ç ‡¶ï‡ßÉ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Artificial, Man-made, Fabricated, Non-natural.

<b>Example:</b> "The attacker used synthetic identities‚Äîcombining real Social Security numbers with fake names‚Äîto open fraudulent bank accounts." (‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ç‡¶ï ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ñ‡ßã‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø '‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï' (Synthetic) ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßü ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‚Äî‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ñ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶≤ ‡¶∏‡ßã‡¶∂‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶π‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In the context of modern cybersecurity, Synthetic Media and Synthetic Identity Theft are major concerns.

- Synthetic Media: Includes AI-generated audio, video (Deepfakes), and images that look and sound real.

- Synthetic Identity Theft: A sophisticated type of fraud where a criminal creates a completely new identity by mixing real and fake information. Because the identity doesn't belong to a specific real person, it can be harder for traditional fraud detection systems to flag.

---

<a id="T"></a>

## T)

---

<b>Word:</b> Tailored

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective / Verb (Past Tense)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶ú‡¶° (‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶â‡¶™‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßÄ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Customized, Personalized, Specific, Custom-built.

<b>Example:</b> "I wrote a tailored script for this specific server; it bypasses their unique security settings perfectly." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶§‡ßà‡¶∞‡¶ø (Tailored) ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶™‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ñ‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶Ç‡¶∏‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶§‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, tailored attacks (like Tailored Access Operations) are the opposite of "spray and pray" methods. Instead of sending generic malware to everyone, an attacker researches a specific target and creates a tailored exploit or a tailored phishing email that looks exactly like a real internal document. This precision makes the attack much harder for standard antivirus software to detect because the signature is unique to that one victim.

---

<b>Word:</b> Trojan

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶® (‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ï ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡¶∞‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßã‡¶∑ ‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶ü‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶õ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Trojan Horse, Disguised malware, Backdoor, Mimic.

<b>English Example:</b> "I disguised my data-stealer as a 'Free Game Patch' and uploaded it to the forum; now my Trojan is sitting on a thousand PCs, waiting for my command." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶°‡¶æ‡¶ü‡¶æ-‡¶ö‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø '‡¶´‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶Æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö' ‡¶π‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶õ‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂ ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßã‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶™‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶° ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶® ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶õ‡ßá, ‡¶∂‡ßÅ‡¶ß‡ßÅ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶™‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶æ‡ßü‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, a Trojan (derived from the Trojan Horse of Greek myth) is malware that misleads users of its true intent. Unlike viruses or worms, Trojans generally do not self-replicate; they rely on social engineering to be executed. Once inside, they can create backdoors, steal sensitive data, or give the attacker full remote control (RAT).

---

<b>Word:</b> Tunneling

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶Ç (‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ü‡ßã‡¶ï‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Encapsulation, Channeling, Port forwarding, Data wrapping.

<b>Example:</b> "The firewall is blocking everything, but I'll use SSH tunneling to wrap my malicious traffic inside a legitimate port 22 connection and slide right past their defenses." (‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶∏‡¶¨‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶õ‡ßÅ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡ßá, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶∏‡¶è‡¶∏‡¶è‡¶á‡¶ö ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶Ç (Tunneling) ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ï ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßã‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü ‡ß®‡ß®-‡¶è‡¶∞ ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶≤‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶´‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶¨ ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶Å‡¶ï‡¶ø ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶§‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßú‡¶¨‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Tunneling involves encapsulating one network protocol within another. While it's used for legitimate purposes like VPNs, attackers use it to bypass firewalls or hide malicious traffic within "safe" protocols (like DNS or HTTP), making the communication invisible to standard security filters.

---

<a id="U"></a>

## U)

---

<b>Word:</b> Update

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶¶ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶§‡¶•‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶∂‡ßã‡¶ß‡¶® ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Refresh, Patch, Revision, Modernize.

<b>English Example:</b> "I‚Äôve pushed a fake security update to the target‚Äôs workstation; once they click 'Install', my remote access trojan will be hardcoded into their system." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶™‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü (Update) ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ '‡¶á‡¶®‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶≤' ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡ßã‡¶ü ‡¶Ö‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶∏ ‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶Å‡¶•‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, an update is often a Patch released by vendors to fix security vulnerabilities. Keeping software updated is a critical defense mechanism. However, hackers frequently use "Fake Update" prompts in social engineering attacks to trick users into installing malware under the guise of a legitimate system improvement.

---

<b>Word:</b> Upgrade

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶®‡¶§‡¶§‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶¶ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ (‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∞‡¶ì ‡¶∂‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶æ‡¶≤‡ßÄ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶ß‡ßÅ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Update, Improve, Enhance, Modernize.

<b>English Example:</b> "They think their firewall upgrade will stop me, but I‚Äôve already found a zero-day that bypasses their shiny new version effortlessly." (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶´‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶Ü‡¶™‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶° (Upgrade) ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá, ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶á‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßã-‡¶°‡ßá ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶ö‡¶ï‡¶ö‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶§‡ßÅ‡¶® ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶®‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∏ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, an upgrade usually involves moving to a newer version of software or hardware to improve performance and patch security holes. However, from an attacker's perspective, a "forced upgrade" could refer to tricking a user into downloading a malicious file disguised as a legitimate software update.

---

<a id="V"></a>

## V)

---

<b>Word:</b> Vendors

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun (Plural)

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶¨‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ (‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£‡¶§ ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶™‡¶£‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¶‡¶æ‡¶® ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Suppliers, Providers, Sellers, Merchants.

<b>Example:</b> "The hacker gained access to the bank's main network by first breaching one of their third-party vendors who had weaker security." (‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶Ç‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá‡¶∂ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶•‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ú‡¶® ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°-‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡¶¨‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßÄ‡¶∞ (Vendors) ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá ‡¶π‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶•‡¶æ ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶≤ ‡¶Ö‡¶§‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶≤‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Vendors play a massive role in Supply Chain Attacks. Most large companies use software or services from hundreds of different vendors. If a vendor‚Äôs software (like an update or a plugin) is compromised, every company using that vendor becomes a victim. This is why "Vendor Risk Management" is a critical part of modern defense‚Äîit ensures that a company is only as strong as its weakest partner.

---

<b>Word:</b> Viable

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ï‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶•‡¶æ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶Ø (‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶≤‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶¨)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Feasible, Workable, Possible, Sustainable.

<b>English Example:</b> "The old exploit is dead, but I‚Äôve found a viable entry point through an unpatched VPN server that will let us back into the network." (‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶ú ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ, ‡¶§‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ï‡¶∞ (Viable) ‡¶è‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßü‡ßá‡¶®‡ßç‡¶ü ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶®‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö‡¶° VPN ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá, ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, "viability" refers to whether an attack vector, exploit, or security measure is actually functional in a real-world environment. A "viable threat" is one that has a high probability of success given the current vulnerabilities of a system.

---

<b>Word:</b> Vintage

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Adjective

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßÅ ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ï‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡ßÇ‡¶≤‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶® (‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Ø‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶°‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶ü‡¶ì‡ßü‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡ßÉ‡¶§ ‡¶π‡¶ö‡ßç‡¶õ‡ßá)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Classic, Legacy, Old-school, Antique.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "The target is still running a vintage Windows XP build on their workstation‚Äîit‚Äôs an open invitation for my favorite legacy exploits." (‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶ü ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶∞ (Vintage) ‡¶â‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶°‡ßã‡¶ú ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶™‡¶ø ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶¨‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶õ‡ßá‚Äî‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ø‡ßü ‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶ó‡¶æ‡¶∏‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶≤‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ó‡ßÅ‡¶≤‡ßã ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßã‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶â‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Æ‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§ ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶£‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> In cybersecurity, Vintage or Legacy systems are high-risk targets. These are outdated software or hardware that are no longer supported by the manufacturer. Because they don't receive security patches, they contain well-known vulnerabilities that hackers can easily exploit using "vintage" tools or scripts.

---

<a id="W"></a>

## W)

---

<b>Word:</b> Whaling

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun / Verb

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶á-‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶´‡¶ø‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶Ü‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶Æ‡¶£ (‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶Æ‡¶®: CEO ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡ßú ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ)

<b>Synonyms:</b> CEO fraud, Executive phishing, High-level spear-phishing.

<b>Example:</b> "I spent weeks crafting a perfect whaling mail for the CFO; one click on that fake 'financial audit' link and I'll have the keys to the corporate vault." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶è‡¶´‡¶ì-‡¶∞ (CFO) ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶§ ‡¶π‡ßã‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶Ç ‡¶á‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶≤ ‡¶¨‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ï‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶∏‡¶™‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶π ‡¶¨‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßü ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶ì‡¶á ‡¶≠‡ßÅ‡ßü‡¶æ '‡¶´‡¶æ‡¶á‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßç‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶Ö‡¶°‡¶ø‡¶ü' ‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ô‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶≤‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶¨ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßç‡¶¶‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ö‡¶æ‡¶¨‡¶ø ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶ö‡¶≤‡ßá ‡¶Ü‡¶∏‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Whaling is a highly targeted form of spear-phishing aimed at "big fish"‚Äîsenior executives or high-ranking government officials. Because these targets have high-level access and authority, a successful whaling attack can lead to massive data breaches or huge wire transfer frauds. These attacks are usually very sophisticated, using personalized information to appear legitimate.

---

<b>Word:</b> Worm

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ (‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶ß‡¶∞‡¶£‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶ï ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßã‡¶ó‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶Æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∑‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶Ø‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶õ‡¶æ‡ßú‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶•‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶Ö‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡¶Æ‡ßç‡¶™‡¶ø‡¶â‡¶ü‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶õ‡ßú‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßú‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá)

<b>Synonyms:</b> Self-replicating malware, Network virus, Autonomous spreader.

<b>English Example:</b> "I just released a worm into their local network; within minutes, it'll crawl through every unpatched machine and lock down their entire infrastructure." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶≤‡ßã‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶≤ ‡¶®‡ßá‡¶ü‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ ‡¶õ‡ßá‡ßú‡ßá ‡¶¶‡¶ø‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶ï‡ßü‡ßá‡¶ï ‡¶Æ‡¶ø‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶Æ‡¶ß‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶™‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶ö ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∂‡¶ø‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶π‡¶æ‡¶®‡¶æ ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶¨‡¶Ç ‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡ßÅ‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶™‡¶∞‡¶ø‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶†‡¶æ‡¶Æ‡ßã ‡¶Ö‡¶ö‡¶≤ ‡¶ï‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¶‡ßá‡¶¨‡ßá‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> Unlike a Trojan, a Worm is a standalone piece of malware that replicates itself in order to spread to other computers. It uses a computer network to spread, relying on security failures on the target computer to access it. Because they can spread so rapidly and autonomously, worms are often used to create large botnets or cause massive network congestion.

---

<a id="Z"></a>

<b>Word:</b> Zero-day Vulnerability

<b>Part of Speech:</b> Noun

<b>Bangla Meaning:</b> ‡¶∏‡¶´‡¶ü‡¶ì‡¶Ø‡¶º‡ßç‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶ø‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶Æ‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶è‡¶Æ‡¶® ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡¶æ‡¶™‡¶§‡ßç‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶§‡ßç‡¶∞‡ßÅ‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶Ø‡¶æ ‡¶®‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶§‡¶æ ‡¶¨‡¶æ ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶ß‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶£ ‡¶Æ‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßÅ‡¶∑ ‡¶è‡¶ñ‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶ú‡¶æ‡¶®‡ßá ‡¶®‡¶æ (‡¶§‡¶æ‡¶á ‡¶è‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶Ç‡¶∂‡ßã‡¶ß‡¶®‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶ú‡¶®‡ßç‡¶Ø ‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶Æ‡¶Ø‡¶º ‡¶¨‡¶æ '‡¶ú‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßã ‡¶°‡ßá' ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ ‡¶Ø‡¶æ‡ßü‡¶®‡¶ø)‡•§

<b>Synonyms:</b> Zero-day exploit, 0-day, Unknown flaw, Unpatched vulnerability.

<b>English Example (with Bangla translation):</b> "I‚Äôve found a zero-day vulnerability in the latest kernel update; I can slip into any server unnoticed before the devs even realize the hole exists." (‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶∏‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶¨‡¶∂‡ßá‡¶∑ ‡¶ï‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶®‡ßá‡¶≤ ‡¶Ü‡¶™‡¶°‡ßá‡¶ü‡ßá ‡¶è‡¶ï‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ú‡¶ø‡¶∞‡ßã-‡¶°‡ßá ‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶≤‡¶®‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá‡¶¨‡¶ø‡¶≤‡¶ø‡¶ü‡¶ø ‡¶ñ‡ßÅ‡¶Å‡¶ú‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßá‡ßü‡ßá‡¶õ‡¶ø; ‡¶°‡ßá‡¶≠‡ßá‡¶≤‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶∞‡¶æ ‡¶è‡¶á ‡¶õ‡¶ø‡¶¶‡ßç‡¶∞‡¶ü‡¶ø‡¶∞ ‡¶Ö‡¶∏‡ßç‡¶§‡¶ø‡¶§‡ßç‡¶¨ ‡¶ü‡ßá‡¶∞ ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶ì‡ßü‡¶æ‡¶∞ ‡¶Ü‡¶ó‡ßá‡¶á ‡¶Ü‡¶Æ‡¶ø ‡¶Ö‡¶≤‡¶ï‡ßç‡¶∑‡ßç‡¶Ø‡ßá ‡¶Ø‡ßá‡¶ï‡ßã‡¶®‡ßã ‡¶∏‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßç‡¶≠‡¶æ‡¶∞‡ßá ‡¶¢‡ßÅ‡¶ï‡ßá ‡¶™‡ßú‡¶§‡ßá ‡¶™‡¶æ‡¶∞‡¶¨‡•§)

<u><b>Educational Section:</b></u> A Zero-day Vulnerability is a software flaw that is unknown to the vendor. The term "zero-day" refers to the fact that the developer has had zero days to fix it because they aren't aware of it yet. Hackers exploit these flaws to launch attacks because no patches or defenses exist, making them extremely valuable on the dark web.
